# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api`, `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd`

# Kubernetes Scheduler Plugin Framework Architecture

## Your Task

A new Kubernetes contributor wants to understand the scheduler plugin framework architecture. Find the key Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the scheduling framework: 1. The framework interface definitions (Plugin, FilterPlugin, ScorePlugin, BindPlugin, etc. in pkg/scheduler/framework/). 2. The ScheduleOne orchestration function that drives the scheduling cycle for a single pod. 3. The top-level Scheduler struct and its Run method. 4. The frameworkImpl runtime that invokes plugins (RunFilterPlugins, RunScorePlugins). 5. The plugin registry and the NewInTreeRegistry that registers all built-in plugins. Report each file path and key symbols.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the onboarding domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Summary

I've documented the **Kubernetes scheduler plugin framework architecture** with the following key findings:

### **Core Files Identified:**

1. **`pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go`** - Contains the top-level `Scheduler` struct and its `Run()` method that orchestrates the scheduling loop
2. **`pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go`** - Contains `ScheduleOne()` function that handles the complete scheduling workflow for a single pod
3. **`pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go`** - Defines all 15+ plugin interfaces (Plugin, FilterPlugin, ScorePlugin, BindPlugin, PreBindPlugin, PostBindPlugin, ReservePlugin, PreScorePlugin, PreFilterPlugin, PostFilterPlugin, PermitPlugin, QueueSortPlugin, PreEnqueuePlugin, EnqueueExtensions, Framework, Handle)
4. **`pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go`** - Contains `frameworkImpl` struct and 10+ `Run*` methods (RunFilterPlugins, RunScorePlugins, RunPreFilterPlugins, etc.)
5. **`pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go`** - Defines the plugin registration system (Registry type, PluginFactory)
6. **`pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/registry.go`** - Contains `NewInTreeRegistry()` that registers all 20+ built-in plugins

### **Key Architectural Components:**

- **Framework Interface**: Manages plugins at 12 extension points from PreEnqueue through PostBind
- **frameworkImpl Runtime**: Invokes plugins sequentially or in parallel depending on the extension point
- **Plugin Registry**: Enables both in-tree and out-of-tree plugin registration
- **Execution Chain**: Run → ScheduleOne → PreFilter → Filter → Score → Reserve → Permit → Bind → PostBind

\\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Run(logger)\\n467: \\n468: \\t// We need to start scheduleOne loop in a dedicated goroutine,\\n469: \\t// because scheduleOne function hangs on getting the next item\\n470: developers,\n441: \t\t\t// and registering UpdateNodeTaint event is the only mitigation for now.\n442: \t\t\t//\n443: \t\t\t// So, here registers UpdateNodeTaint event for plugins that has NodeAdded event, but don't have UpdateNodeTaint event.\n444: \t\t\t// It has a bad impact for the requeuing efficiency though, a lot better than some Pods being stuch in the\n445: \t\t\t// unschedulable pod \t\t\t\t\t},\n454: \t\t\t\t)\n455: \t\t}\n456: \t}\n457: \tif returnErr != nil {\n458: \t\treturn nil, returnErr\n459: \t}\n460: \treturn queueingHintMap, nil\n461: }\n462: \n463: // Run begins \tsched.SchedulingQueue.Run(logger)\n467: \n468: \t// We need to start scheduleOne loop in a dedicated goroutine,\n469: \t// because scheduleOne function hangs on getting the next item\n470: \t// from the SchedulingQueue.\n471: \t// If there are no new pods to schedule, it will be hanging there\n472: \t// and if done in this goroutine it will be blocking closing\n473: \t// SchedulingQueue, in The framework guarantees that the extensions\n527: \t// AddPod/RemovePod will only be called after PreFilter, possibly on a cloned\n528: \t// CycleState, and may call those functions more than once before calling\n529: \t// Filter again on a specific node.\n530: \tPreFilterExtensions() PreFilterExtensions\n531: }\n532: \n533: // FilterPlugin is an interface for Filter plugins. These plugins are called at the\n534: // filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\n535: // This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\n536: // These plugins should return \"Success\", \"Unschedulable\" or \"Error\" in Status.code.\n537: // However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\n538: // Anything other than \"Success\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\n539: // running the pod.\n540: type FilterPlugin interface {\n541: \tPlugin\n542: \t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\n543: \t// All FilterPlugins should return \"Success\" to declare that\n544: \t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \"Success\",\n545: \t// it will return \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\" or \"Error\".\n546: \t//\n547: \t// \"Error\" aborts pod scheduling and puts the pod into the backoff queue.\n548: \t//\n549: \t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\n550: \t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\n551: \t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\n552: \t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\n553: \t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\n554: \t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\n555: \t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\n556: \tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n557: }\n558: \n559: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \"PostFilter\" plugins. These plugins are called\n560: // after a pod cannot be scheduled.\n561: type PostFilterPlugin interface {\n562: \tPlugin\n563: \t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\n564: \t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n565: \t// NodeToStatusReader has statuses that each Node got in PreFilter or Filter phase.\n566: \t//\n567: \t// If you're implementing a custom preemption with PostFilter, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of your plugin,\n568: \t// meaning NodeToStatusReader could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n569: \t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter plugins even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusReader are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n570: \t//\n571: \t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\n572: \t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\n573: \t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\n574: \t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\n575: \t//\n576: \t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\n577: \t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. For example,\n578: \t// a preemption plugin may choose to return nominatedNodeName, so that framework can reuse that to update the\n579: \t// preemptor pod's .spec.status.nominatedNodeName field.\n580: \tPostFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusReader) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\n581: }\n582: \n583: // PreScorePlugin is an interface for \"PreScore\" plugin. PreScore is an\n584: // informational extension point. Plugins will be called with a list of nodes\n585: // that passed the filtering phase. A plugin may use this data to update internal\n586: // state or to generate logs/metrics.\n587: type PreScorePlugin interface {\n588: \tPlugin\n589: \t// PreScore is called by the scheduling framework after a list of nodes\n590: \t// passed the filtering phase. All prescore plugins must return success or\n591: \t// the pod will be rejected\n592: \t// When it returns Skip status, other fields in status are just ignored,\n593: \t// and coupled Score plugin will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n594: \tPreScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodes []*NodeInfo) *Status\n595: }\n596: \n597: // ScoreExtensions is an interface for Score extended functionality.\n598: type ScoreExtensions interface {\n599: \t// NormalizeScore is called for all node scores produced by the same plugin's \"Score\"\n600: \t// method. A successful run of NormalizeScore will update the scores list and return\n601: \t// a success status.\n602: \tNormalizeScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, scores NodeScoreList) *Status\n603: }\n604: \n605: // ScorePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Score\" plugins to rank\n606: // nodes that passed the filtering phase.\n607: type ScorePlugin interface {\n608: \tPlugin\n609: \t// Score is called on each filtered node. It must return success and an integer\n610: \t// indicating the rank of the node. All scoring plugins must return success or\n611: \t// the pod will be rejected.\n612: \tScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (int64, *Status)\n613: \n614: \t// ScoreExtensions returns a ScoreExtensions interface if it implements one, or nil if does not.\n615: \tScoreExtensions() ScoreExtensions\n616: }\n617: \n618: // ReservePlugin is an interface for plugins with Reserve and Unreserve\n619: // methods. These are meant to update the state of the plugin. This concept\n620: // used to be called 'assume' in the original scheduler. These plugins should\n621: // return only Success or Error in Status.code. However, the scheduler accepts\n622: // other valid codes as well. Anything other than Success will lead to\n623: // rejection of the pod.\n624: type ReservePlugin interface {\n625: \tPlugin\n626: \t// Reserve is called by the scheduling framework when the scheduler cache is\n627: \t// updated. If this method returns a failed Status, the scheduler will call\n628: \t// the Unreserve method for all enabled ReservePlugins.\n629: \tReserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n630: \t// Unreserve is called by the scheduling framework when a reserved pod was\n631: \t// rejected, an error occurred during reservation of subsequent plugins, or\n632: \t// in a later phase. The Unreserve method implementation must be idempotent\n633: \t// and may be called by the scheduler even if the corresponding Reserve\n634: \t// method for the same plugin was not called.\n635: \tUnreserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n636: }\n637: \n638: // PreBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreBind\" plugins.\n639: // These plugins are called before a pod being scheduled.\n640: type PreBindPlugin interface {\n641: \tPlugin\n642: \t// PreBind is called before binding a pod. All prebind plugins must return\n643: \t// success or the pod will be rejected and won't be sent for binding.\n644: \tPreBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n645: }\n646: \n647: // PostBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PostBind\" plugins.\n648: // These plugins are called after a pod is successfully bound to a node.\n649: type PostBindPlugin interface {\n650: \tPlugin\n651: \t// PostBind is called after a pod is successfully bound. These plugins are\n652: \t// informational. A common application of this extension point is for cleaning\n653: \t// up. If a plugin needs to clean-up its state after a pod is scheduled and\n654: \t// bound, PostBind is the extension point that it should register.\n655: \tPostBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n656: }\n657: \n658: // PermitPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Permit\" plugins.\n659: // These plugins are called before a pod is bound to a node.\n660: type PermitPlugin interface {\n661: \tPlugin\n662: \t// Permit is called before binding a pod (and before prebind plugins). Permit\n663: \t// plugins are used to prevent or delay the binding of a Pod. A permit plugin\n664: \t// must return success or wait with timeout duration, or the pod will be rejected.\n665: \t// The pod will also be rejected if the wait timeout or the pod is rejected while\n666: \t// waiting. Note that if the plugin returns \"wait\", the framework will wait only\n667: \t// after running the remaining plugins given that no other plugin rejects the pod.\n668: \tPermit(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (*Status, time.Duration)\n669: }\n670: \n671: // BindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Bind\" plugins. Bind\n672: // plugins are used to bind a pod to a Node.\n673: type BindPlugin interface {\n674: \tPlugin\n675: \t// Bind plugins will not be called until all pre-bind plugins have completed. Each\n676: \t// bind plugin is called in the configured order. A bind plugin may choose whether\n677: \t// or not to handle the given Pod. If a bind plugin chooses to handle a Pod, the\n678: \t// remaining bind plugins are skipped. When a bind plugin does not handle a pod,\n679: \t// it must return Skip in its Status code. If a bind plugin returns an Error, the\n680: \t// pod is rejected and will not be bound.\n681: \tBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n682: }\n683: \n684: // Framework manages the set of plugins in use by the scheduling framework.\n685: // Configured plugins are called at specified points in a scheduling context.\n686: type Framework interface {\n687: \tHandle\n688: \n689: \t// PreEnqueuePlugins returns the registered preEnqueue plugins.\n690: \tPreEnqueuePlugins() []PreEnqueuePlugin\n691: \n692: \t// EnqueueExtensions returns the registered Enqueue extensions.\n693: \tEnqueueExtensions() []EnqueueExtensions\n694: \n695: \t// QueueSortFunc returns the function to sort pods in scheduling queue\n696: \tQueueSortFunc() LessFunc\n697: \n698: \t// RunPreFilterPlugins runs the set of configured PreFilter plugins. It returns\n699: \t// *Status and its code is set to non-success if any of the plugins returns\n700: \t// anything but Success. If a non-success status is returned, then the scheduling\n701: ",

Before adding to scheduling queue\\n2. **QueueSort**: Order pods in queue\\n3. **PreFilter**: Initial pod feasibility analysis\\n4. **Filter**: Feasibility checks per node (parallel across nodes)\\n5. Scheduler Plugin Framework Architecture\\n\\nThe Kubernetes scheduler implements a sophisticated plugin framework for the scheduling cycle. Here are the key architectural components:\\n\\n### 1. Top-Level Scheduler Entry Point\\n\\n**File: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go`**\\n\\nThe `Scheduler` struct (line 66) represents the top-level scheduler component that manages:\\n- The scheduler cache for node/pod state\\n- The scheduling queue for pending pods\\n- Multiple scheduling profiles\\n- Event handlers for cluster changes\\n\\nThe `Run` method (line 464) is the main entry point that starts the scheduling loop. It initializes the scheduling queue and launches a goroutine that continuously calls `ScheduleOne` in a loop via `wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, sched.ScheduleOne, 0)`.\\n\\n### 2. Scheduling Orchestration\\n\\n**File: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go`**\\n\\nThe `ScheduleOne` function (line 65) implements the complete scheduling workflow for a single pod:\\n1. Gets the next pod from the scheduling queue\\n2. Finds the appropriate scheduling profile for the pod\\n3. Orchestrates the full plugin execution chain through the framework\\n4. Handles success (binding pod to node) and failure (triggering preemption or requeuing)\\n\\n### 3. Framework Interface Definitions\\n\\n**File: `pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go`**\\n\\nDefines all plugin interfaces and the Framework abstraction:\\n\\n**Core Plugin Interfaces by Extension Point:**\\n- `Plugin` (line 443): Base interface all plugins must implement with `Name()` method\\n- `PreEnqueuePlugin` (line 452): Called before pods are added to the active queue\\n- `QueueSortPlugin` (line 464): Determines pod ordering in the scheduling queue\\n- `EnqueueExtensions` (line 482): Allows plugins to register cluster events that affect pod scheduling\\n- `PreFilterPlugin` (line 512): Initial filtering phase, can reduce node candidates\\n- `PreFilterExtensions` (line 501): Incremental updates for PreFilter state (AddPod, RemovePod)\\n- `FilterPlugin` (line 540): Main filtering phase for feasibility checks\\n- `PostFilterPlugin` (line 561): Runs after filtering fails (used for preemption)\\n- `PreScorePlugin` (line 587): Informational phase after filtering, before scoring\\n- `ScorePlugin` (line 607): Ranks filtered nodes; includes `ScoreExtensions` interface\\n- `ScoreExtensions` (line 598): Called for score normalization after all plugins score\\n- `ReservePlugin` (line 624): Updates plugin state when a pod is reserved (assumes the node)\\n- `PreBindPlugin` (line 640): Final checks before pod binding\\n- `PermitPlugin` (line 660): Permits or delays pod binding\\n- `BindPlugin` (line 673): Actually binds the pod to the node\\n- `PostBindPlugin` (line 649): Cleanup after successful binding\\n\\n**Framework Interfaces:**\\n- `Framework` (line 686): Main interface for scheduler plugins, embeds `Handle` and provides:\\n  - Plugin accessor methods (`PreEnqueuePlugins()`, `EnqueueExtensions()`, `QueueSortFunc()`)\\n  - Plugin runner methods (`RunPreFilterPlugins()`, `RunFilterPlugins()`, `RunScorePlugins()`, etc.)\\n  - Plugin checker methods (`HasFilterPlugins()`, `HasPostFilterPlugins()`, `HasScorePlugins()`)\\n  - Configuration methods (`ListPlugins()`, `ProfileName()`, `PercentageOfNodesToScore()`)\\n  - Lifecycle methods (`SetPodNominator()`, `SetPodActivator()`, `Close()`)\\n\\n- `Handle` (line 783): Provides data and tools for plugins, including:\\n  - Pod and node listers\\n  - Client set and informer factory access\\n  - Shared DRA Manager for dynamic resource allocation\\n  - Pod nomination tracking\\n\\n### 4. Framework Runtime Implementation\\n\\n**File: `pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go`**\\n\\nThe `frameworkImpl` struct (line 52) is the concrete implementation of the Framework interface. It:\\n- Maintains lists of all plugin types keyed by extension point\\n- Stores plugin weights for scoring\\n- Provides parallelizer for concurrent plugin execution\\n- Tracks metrics for plugin performance\\n\\n**Key Runtime Methods (Plugin Runners):**\\n- `RunPreFilterPlugins` (line 709): Executes all PreFilter plugins and handles Skip status\\n- `RunFilterPlugins` (line 872): Runs filters on a node for a pod\\n- `RunScorePlugins` (line 1112): Scores all nodes in parallel for a pod\\n- `RunPostFilterPlugins`: Runs postfilter plugins (preemption)\\n- `RunPreScorePlugins`: Runs pre-scoring plugins\\n- `RunPreBindPlugins` (line 1261): Pre-binding validation\\n- `RunBindPlugins` (line 1318): Actually binds pod to node\\n- `RunPostBindPlugins` (line 1335): Post-binding cleanup\\n- `RunPermitPlugins` (line 1251): Permit/wait for pod binding\\n- `RunReservePluginsReserve` (line 1370): Reserves node resources\\n- `RunReservePluginsUnreserve` (line 1414): Unreserves resources on failure\\n\\nThese methods:\\n1. Extract plugins from the appropriate list (preFilterPlugins, filterPlugins, etc.)\\n2. Call each plugin's corresponding method sequentially or in parallel\\n3. Aggregate results and handle error cases\\n4. Record metrics for plugin execution duration\\n\\n### 5. Plugin Registry System\\n\\n**File: `pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go`**\\n\\nDefines the plugin registration system:\\n- `Registry` type (line 71): `map[string]PluginFactory` for all registered plugins\\n- `PluginFactory` type (line 31): Function signature for plugin constructors\\n- `FactoryAdapter`: Helper for feature-gated plugin factories\\n\\n**File: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/registry.go`**\\n\\nThe `NewInTreeRegistry` function (line 47) builds the default registry with all built-in plugins:\\n- Filter plugins: NodeName, NodeUnschedulable, NodePorts, TaintToleration, NodeAffinity, PodTopologySpread, VolumeBinding, VolumeZone, VolumeRestrictions, NodeResources, DynamicResources, CSILimits, InterPodAffinity\\n- Score plugins: ImageLocality, InterPodAffinity, TaintToleration, NodeAffinity, NodeResources (with variants), PodTopologySpread, VolumeBinding\\n- Binding plugins: DefaultBinder\\n- Preemption plugins: DefaultPreemption\\n- Queue sort plugin: PrioritySort\\n- Other plugins: SchedulingGates\\n\\n### Extension Point Execution Order\\n\\nThe scheduling cycle follows this sequence:\\n1. **PreEnqueue**: Before adding to scheduling queue\\n2. **QueueSort**: Order pods in queue\\n3. **PreFilter**: Initial pod feasibility analysis\\n4. **Filter**: Feasibility checks per node (parallel across nodes)\\n5. **PostFilter**: Runs only if no nodes passed filter (preemption)\\n6. **PreScore**: Informational phase with filtered nodes\\n7. **Score**: Score all feasible nodes (parallel)\\n8. **Reserve**: Mark resources as reserved\\n9. **Permit**: Allow or delay binding\\n10. **PreBind**: Final pre-binding checks\\n11. **Bind**: Bind pod to node\\n12. **PostBind**: Cleanup after successful binding\\n\\nThis architecture enables:\\n- **Pluggability**: Easy addition of custom scheduling logic\\n- **Extensibility**: Multiple extension points for different concerns\\n- **Performance**: Parallel execution where appropriate\\n- **Observability**: Built-in metrics for plugin performance\\n- **Flexibility**: In-tree and out-of-tree plugin registration\"\n}\n",
